AISafetyBenchExplorer: A Metric-Aware Catalogue of AI Safety Benchmarks Reveals Fragmented Measurement and Weak Benchmark Governance
Authors: Abiodun A. Solanke
First: 2026-04-14T15:26:03+00:00 · Latest: 2026-04-23T13:27:05+00:00
Comments: This paper has been withdrawn by the author while an institutional affiliation compliance matter is under review. It may be resubmitted once the matter is resolved
Abs · PDF · Code1 · Code2
Abstract
The rapid expansion of large language model (LLM) safety evaluation has produced a substantial benchmark ecosystem, but not a correspondingly coherent measurement ecosystem. We present AISafetyBenchExplorer, a structured catalogue of 195 AI safety benchmarks released between 2018 and 2026, organized through a multi-sheet schema that records benchmark-level metadata, metric-level definitions, benchmark-paper metadata, and repository activity. This design enables meta-analysis not only of what benchmarks exist, but also of how safety is operationalized, aggregated, and judged across the literature. Using the updated catalogue, we identify a central structural problem: benchmark proliferation has outpaced measurement standardization. The current landscape is dominated by medium-complexity benchmarks (94/195), while only 7 benchmarks occupy the Popular tier. The workbook further reports strong concentration around English-only evaluation (165/195), evaluation-only resources (170/195), stale GitHub repositories (137/195), stale Hugging Face datasets (96/195), and heavy reliance on arXiv preprints among benchmarks with known venue metadata. At the metric level, the catalogue shows that familiar labels such as accuracy, F1 score, safety score, and aggregate benchmark scores often conceal materially different judges, aggregation rules, and threat models. We argue that the field's main failure mode is fragmentation rather than scarcity. Researchers now have many benchmark artifacts, but they often lack a shared measurement language, a principled basis for benchmark selection, and durable stewardship norms for post publication maintenance. AISafetyBenchExplorer addresses this gap by providing a traceable benchmark catalogue, a controlled metadata schema, and a complexity taxonomy that together support more rigorous benchmark discovery, comparison, and meta-evaluation.
中文标题/摘要
标题：AISafetyBenchExplorer：一个关注指标的AI安全基准目录揭示了测量的碎片化和基准治理的薄弱
大型语言模型（LLM）安全评估的快速扩展产生了一个庞大的基准生态系统，但没有相应连贯的测量生态系统。我们提出了AISafetyBenchExplorer，这是一个结构化的目录，包含2018年至2026年间发布的195个AI安全基准，采用多表格模式记录基准级元数据、指标级定义、基准论文元数据和仓库活动。该设计不仅支持对现有基准的元分析，还支持对安全如何在文献中被操作、聚合和评判的分析。使用更新的目录，我们识别出一个核心结构性问题：基准的激增超过了测量标准化。目前的格局以中等复杂度的基准为主（94/195），而只有7个基准位于流行层级。工作簿进一步报告了对仅英语评估（165/195）、仅评估资源（170/195）、过时的GitHub仓库（137/195）、过时的Hugging Face数据集（96/195）以及在已知场地元数据的基准中对arXiv预印本的高度依赖的强烈集中。在指标层面，目录显示，诸如准确性、F1分数、安全分数和聚合基准分数等熟悉标签常常掩盖了实质上不同的评判者、聚合规则和威胁模型。我们认为，该领域的主要失败模式是碎片化而非稀缺。研究人员现在拥有许多基准文物，但通常缺乏共享的测量语言、基准选择的原则基础以及发布后维护的持久管理规范。AISafetyBenchExplorer通过提供可追溯的基准目录、受控的元数据模式和复杂性分类法来填补这一空白，从而支持更严格的基准发现、比较和元评估。
Summary / 总结
The research addresses the fragmented landscape of AI safety benchmarks, which has emerged alongside the rapid growth of large language model safety evaluations. Previous methods have led to a proliferation of benchmarks without a coherent measurement framework, resulting in issues such as a lack of standardization and heavy reliance on English-only evaluations. The proposed AISafetyBenchExplorer offers a structured catalogue of 195 AI safety benchmarks, organized with a multi-sheet schema that captures benchmark metadata and metric definitions, thereby facilitating meta-analysis and addressing the fragmentation problem. This contribution enables researchers to discover, compare, and evaluate benchmarks more rigorously, ultimately supporting the establishment of a shared measurement language and better stewardship practices in the field. The methodology includes a comprehensive analysis of existing benchmarks and their metrics, revealing a dominance of medium-complexity benchmarks and highlighting the need for improved measurement standards.
本研究针对随着大型语言模型安全评估的快速发展而出现的AI安全基准的碎片化现象。以往的方法导致基准的激增，但缺乏一致的测量框架，造成标准化不足和资源集中在仅用英语评估的问题。提出的AISafetyBenchExplorer提供了一个结构化的195个AI安全基准的目录，配有详细的元数据和复杂性分类法，便于更好地发现和比较基准。该贡献旨在统一测量语言并改善基准生态系统的治理。该方法论包括一个多表格架构，捕捉基准级和指标级信息，揭示大多数基准为中等复杂性，并强调在AI研究中对安全评估采取更标准化方法的必要性。
Secure LLM Fine-Tuning via Safety-Aware Probing
Authors: Chengcan Wu, Zhixin Zhang, Zeming Wei, Yihao Zhang, Xiaokun Luan, Meng Sun
First: 2025-05-22T14:52:10+00:00 · Latest: 2026-04-23T08:31:23+00:00
Abs · PDF · Code1 · Code2 · Code3
Abstract
Large language models (LLMs) have achieved remarkable success across many applications, but their ability to generate harmful content raises serious safety concerns. Although safety alignment techniques are often applied during pre-training or post-training, recent studies show that subsequent fine-tuning on adversarial or even benign data can still compromise model safety. In this paper, we revisit the fundamental question of why fine-tuning on non-harmful data may nevertheless degrade safety. We show that the safety and task-performance loss landscapes are partially decoupled, so updates that improve task-specific performance may still move the model toward unsafe regions. Based on this insight, we propose a safety-aware probing (SAP) optimization framework for mitigating safety risks during fine-tuning. Concretely, SAP uses contrastive safety signals to locate safety-correlated directions, and optimizes a lightweight probe that perturbs hidden-state propagation during fine-tuning, thereby steering parameter updates away from harmful trajectories while preserving task-specific learning. Extensive experiments show that SAP consistently improves the safety--utility tradeoff across multiple models and tasks. Averaged over multiple LLMs, SAP reduces the harmful score significantly relative to standard fine-tuning, outperforming strong baselines while maintaining competitive task-specific performance. SAP also demonstrates stronger robustness under harmful data poisoning, adversarial fine-tuning, and a dedicated post-fine-tuning adaptive attack, validating that SAP is an effective and scalable framework for preserving LLM safety during fine-tuning. Our code is available at https://github.com/ChengcanWu/SAP.
中文标题/摘要
标题：通过安全感知探测进行安全的LLM微调
大型语言模型（LLMs）在许多应用中取得了显著成功，但其生成有害内容的能力引发了严重的安全担忧。尽管安全对齐技术通常在预训练或后训练期间应用，但最近的研究表明，随后在对抗性或甚至良性数据上的微调仍然可能危及模型安全。本文重新审视了一个基本问题，即为什么在无害数据上的微调仍可能降低安全性。我们表明，安全性和任务性能损失的景观部分解耦，因此改善任务特定性能的更新可能仍会将模型推向不安全区域。基于这一见解，我们提出了一种安全感知探测（SAP）优化框架，以减轻微调过程中的安全风险。具体而言，SAP使用对比安全信号来定位与安全相关的方向，并优化一个轻量级探测器，在微调过程中扰动隐藏状态传播，从而将参数更新引导远离有害轨迹，同时保持任务特定学习。大量实验表明，SAP在多个模型和任务中始终改善安全性与效用的权衡。在多个LLM上平均，SAP相对于标准微调显著降低了有害评分，超越了强基线，同时保持了竞争性的任务特定性能。SAP在有害数据中毒、对抗性微调和专门的后微调自适应攻击下也表现出更强的鲁棒性，验证了SAP是一个有效且可扩展的框架，用于在微调过程中保持LLM的安全性。我们的代码可在https://github.com/ChengcanWu/SAP获取。
Summary / 总结
The research addresses the safety concerns associated with large language models (LLMs), particularly how fine-tuning on non-harmful data can still lead to safety degradation. Previous methods focused on safety alignment during pre-training or post-training but failed to prevent safety risks during fine-tuning, as improvements in task performance could inadvertently lead models toward unsafe regions. This paper proposes a safety-aware probing (SAP) optimization framework that utilizes contrastive safety signals to identify safety-correlated directions and optimizes a lightweight probe to adjust hidden-state propagation during fine-tuning, thus steering updates away from harmful trajectories while maintaining task performance. The contribution of this work is the demonstration that SAP significantly enhances the safety-utility tradeoff across various models and tasks, achieving a notable reduction in harmful scores compared to standard fine-tuning while preserving competitive task-specific performance, and showing robustness against harmful data poisoning and adversarial attacks.
本研究关注大型语言模型（LLMs）所带来的安全隐患，特别是如何在非有害数据上进行微调仍可能导致安全性下降。以往的方法主要集中在预训练或后训练期间的安全对齐，但未能考虑微调过程中安全性与任务性能的解耦，导致潜在风险。所提出的安全感知探测（SAP）框架通过使用对比安全信号来引导更新远离有害区域，同时保持任务性能，从而改进了这些方法。该方法的提出是合理的，因为它直接解决了现有方法中的问题。本文的贡献在于证明SAP在多个模型和任务中增强了安全性与效用的权衡，相较于标准微调显著降低了有害评分，同时保持了竞争性的任务特定性能，从而验证了其在有害数据场景下的有效性和可扩展性。
Logic Jailbreak: Efficiently Unlocking LLM Safety Restrictions Through Formal Logical Expression
Authors: Jingyu Peng, Maolin Wang, Nan Wang, Jiatong Li, Yuchen Li, Yuyang Ye, Wanyu Wang, Pengyue Jia, Kai Zhang, Xiangyu Zhao
First: 2025-05-18T04:23:51+00:00 · Latest: 2026-04-23T06:18:23+00:00
Abs · PDF · Code1 · Code2
Abstract
Despite substantial advancements in aligning large language models (LLMs) with human values, current safety mechanisms remain susceptible to jailbreak attacks. We hypothesize that this vulnerability stems from distributional discrepancies between alignment-oriented prompts and malicious prompts. To investigate this, we introduce LogiBreak, a novel and universal black-box jailbreak method that leverages logical expression translation to circumvent LLM safety systems. By converting harmful natural language prompts into formal logical expressions, LogiBreak exploits the distributional gap between alignment data and logic-based inputs, preserving the underlying semantic intent and readability while evading safety constraints. We evaluate LogiBreak on a multilingual jailbreak dataset spanning three languages, demonstrating its effectiveness across various evaluation settings and linguistic contexts.
中文标题/摘要
标题：逻辑越狱：通过形式逻辑表达高效解锁大型语言模型安全限制
尽管在将大型语言模型（LLMs）与人类价值观对齐方面取得了重大进展，但当前的安全机制仍然容易受到越狱攻击。我们假设这种脆弱性源于对齐导向提示与恶意提示之间的分布差异。为此，我们引入了LogiBreak，这是一种新颖且通用的黑箱越狱方法，利用逻辑表达翻译来规避LLM安全系统。通过将有害的自然语言提示转换为形式逻辑表达，LogiBreak利用对齐数据与基于逻辑的输入之间的分布差距，保持潜在的语义意图和可读性，同时规避安全约束。我们在涵盖三种语言的多语言越狱数据集上评估LogiBreak，展示了其在各种评估设置和语言环境中的有效性。
Summary / 总结
The research addresses the ongoing challenge of jailbreak attacks on large language models (LLMs), which have made significant progress in aligning with human values but still exhibit vulnerabilities in their safety mechanisms. Previous methods have struggled with distributional discrepancies between alignment-oriented prompts and malicious inputs, leading to ineffective safety measures. The proposed approach, LogiBreak, introduces a universal black-box jailbreak method that translates harmful natural language prompts into formal logical expressions, effectively exploiting the identified distributional gap while maintaining semantic intent and readability. This method is well-motivated as it directly targets the weaknesses of existing safety systems. The paper contributes by demonstrating LogiBreak's effectiveness on a multilingual jailbreak dataset across three languages, achieving robust performance in various evaluation settings and supporting the goal of enhancing LLM safety.
本文探讨了确保大型语言模型（LLMs）安全性的持续挑战，尽管在与人类价值观对齐方面取得了进展，但仍然容易受到越狱攻击。以往的方法在对齐导向和恶意提示之间的分布差异上存在问题，导致安全机制效果不佳。提出的方法LogiBreak引入了一种新颖的黑箱越狱方法，通过将有害的自然语言提示转换为形式逻辑表达，有效弥合了分布差距，同时保持语义意图，绕过安全限制。本文的贡献在于展示LogiBreak在跨三种语言的多语言越狱数据集上的有效性，在各种评估设置中取得显著的性能提升，从而支持增强LLM安全性的目标。
LASA: Language-Agnostic Semantic Alignment at the Semantic Bottleneck for LLM Safety
Authors: Junxiao Yang, Haoran Liu, Jinzhe Tu, Jiale Cheng, Zhexin Zhang, Shiyao Cui, Jiaqi Weng, Jialing Tao, Hui Xue, Hongning Wang, Han Qiu, Minlie Huang
First: 2026-04-13T15:59:50+00:00 · Latest: 2026-04-23T04:47:08+00:00
Abs · PDF · Code1 · Code2
Abstract
Large language models (LLMs) often demonstrate strong safety performance in high-resource languages, yet exhibit severe vulnerabilities when queried in low-resource languages. We attribute this gap to a mismatch between language-agnostic semantic understanding ability and language-dominant safety alignment biased toward high-resource languages. Consistent with this hypothesis, we empirically identify the semantic bottleneck in LLMs, an intermediate layer in which the geometry of model representations is governed primarily by shared semantic content rather than language identity. Building on this observation, we propose Language-Agnostic Semantic Alignment (LASA), which anchors safety alignment directly in semantic bottlenecks. Experiments show that LASA substantially improves safety across all languages: average attack success rate (ASR) drops from 24.7% to 2.8% on LLaMA-3.1-8B-Instruct and remains around 3-4% across Qwen2.5 and Qwen3 Instruct models (7B-32B). Together, our analysis and method offer a representation-level perspective on LLM safety, suggesting that safety alignment requires anchoring safety understanding not in surface text, but in the model's language-agnostic semantic space.
中文标题/摘要
标题：LASA：在语义瓶颈处实现语言无关的语义对齐以提高大型语言模型的安全性
大型语言模型（LLMs）在高资源语言中通常表现出强大的安全性能，但在低资源语言中查询时却表现出严重的脆弱性。我们将这一差距归因于语言无关的语义理解能力与偏向高资源语言的语言主导安全对齐之间的不匹配。与这一假设一致，我们实证识别了LLMs中的语义瓶颈，这是一个中间层，其中模型表示的几何形状主要由共享的语义内容而非语言身份所主导。基于这一观察，我们提出了语言无关的语义对齐（LASA），直接在语义瓶颈中锚定安全对齐。实验表明，LASA显著提高了所有语言的安全性：在LLaMA-3.1-8B-Instruct上的平均攻击成功率（ASR）从24.7%降至2.8%，在Qwen2.5和Qwen3 Instruct模型（7B-32B）中保持在3-4%左右。我们的分析和方法共同提供了对LLM安全性的表示级视角，表明安全对齐需要将安全理解锚定在模型的语言无关语义空间中，而非表面文本中。
Summary / 总结
The research addresses the safety performance discrepancies of large language models (LLMs) between high-resource and low-resource languages, identifying a semantic bottleneck where model representations are influenced more by shared semantic content than by language identity. Previous methods have focused on language-specific safety alignment, which has proven inadequate for low-resource languages, leading to vulnerabilities. The proposed Language-Agnostic Semantic Alignment (LASA) method directly anchors safety alignment in these semantic bottlenecks, effectively bridging the gap between semantic understanding and safety across languages. The methodology involves empirical analysis of LLM representations and the implementation of LASA, which has demonstrated a significant reduction in average attack success rates from 24.7% to 2.8% on LLaMA-3.1-8B-Instruct and maintains low rates around 3-4% for other models, thus supporting the goal of enhancing LLM safety universally.
本研究关注大型语言模型（LLMs）在高资源语言和低资源语言之间的安全性能差异，识别出语义瓶颈，即模型表示主要受语义内容而非语言身份的影响。以往的方法侧重于语言特定的安全对齐，但在低资源语言中效果不佳。提出的语言无关语义对齐（LASA）方法直接将安全对齐锚定在这些语义瓶颈中，有效弥补了安全性能的差距。本文通过强调语义理解的重要性而非语言特定特征，为LLM安全性提供了一种新颖的视角。该方法论包括实证分析和LASA的实施，显著降低了LLaMA-3.1-8B-Instruct的平均攻击成功率，从24.7%降至2.8%，并在其他模型中保持低水平，证明该方法有效提升了多种语言的安全性。
Dialect vs Demographics: Quantifying LLM Bias from Implicit Linguistic Signals vs. Explicit User Profiles
Authors: Irti Haq, Belén Saldías
First: 2026-04-22T23:33:18+00:00 · Latest: 2026-04-22T23:33:18+00:00
Comments: In The 2026 ACM Conference on Fairness, Accountability, and Transparency (FAccT '26), June 25--28, 2026, Montreal, Canada. ACM, New York, NY, USA, 32 pages
Abs · PDF · Code1 · Code2
Abstract
As state-of-the-art Large Language Models (LLMs) have become ubiquitous, ensuring equitable performance across diverse demographics is critical. However, it remains unclear whether these disparities arise from the explicitly stated identity itself or from the way identity is signaled. In real-world interactions, users' identity is often conveyed implicitly through a complex combination of various socio-linguistic factors. This study disentangles these signals by employing a factorial design with over 24,000 responses from two open-weight LLMs (Gemma-3-12B and Qwen-3-VL-8B), comparing prompts with explicitly announced user profiles against implicit dialect signals (e.g., AAVE, Singlish) across various sensitive domains. Our results uncover a unique paradox in LLM safety where users achieve ``better'' performance by sounding like a demographic than by stating they belong to it. Explicit identity prompts activate aggressive safety filters, increasing refusal rates and reducing semantic similarity compared to our reference text for Black users. In contrast, implicit dialect cues trigger a powerful ``dialect jailbreak,'' reducing refusal probability to near zero while simultaneously achieving a greater level of semantic similarity to the reference texts compared to Standard American English prompts. However, this ``dialect jailbreak'' introduces a critical safety trade-off regarding content sanitization. We find that current safety alignment techniques are brittle and over-indexed on explicit keywords, creating a bifurcated user experience where ``standard'' users receive cautious, sanitized information while dialect speakers navigate a less sanitized, more raw, and potentially a more hostile information landscape and highlights a fundamental tension in alignment--between equitable and linguistic diversity--and underscores the need for safety mechanisms that generalize beyond explicit cues.
中文标题/摘要
标题：方言与人口统计：量化隐性语言信号与显性用户档案中的LLM偏见
随着最先进的大型语言模型（LLMs）变得无处不在，确保在不同人口统计中公平的表现至关重要。然而，这些差异是否源于明确声明的身份本身，还是身份信号的方式仍不清楚。在现实互动中，用户的身份通常通过各种社会语言因素的复杂组合隐性传达。本研究通过采用因子设计，分析来自两个开放权重LLM（Gemma-3-12B和Qwen-3-VL-8B）的超过24,000个响应，比较显性用户档案的提示与隐性方言信号（例如，AAVE，Singlish）在各个敏感领域的表现。我们的结果揭示了LLM安全性中的一个独特悖论，即用户通过听起来像某个群体而不是明确声明自己属于该群体来获得“更好”的表现。显性身份提示激活了激进的安全过滤器，增加了拒绝率，并减少了与黑人用户参考文本的语义相似性。相比之下，隐性方言线索触发了强大的“方言越狱”，将拒绝概率降低到接近零，同时与参考文本相比，达到了更高的语义相似性。然而，这种“方言越狱”引入了关于内容净化的关键安全权衡。我们发现当前的安全对齐技术脆弱，并过度依赖显性关键词，造成了“标准”用户获得谨慎、净化的信息，而方言使用者则在一个较少净化、更原始且可能更具敌意的信息环境中导航，突显了对齐中的基本紧张关系——在公平性与语言多样性之间——并强调了需要超越显性线索的安全机制。
Summary / 总结
The research addresses the critical issue of bias in Large Language Models (LLMs) related to demographic disparities, focusing on whether these biases stem from explicit user profiles or implicit linguistic signals. Previous methods have primarily relied on explicit identity prompts, which have been shown to activate aggressive safety filters, leading to increased refusal rates and reduced semantic similarity for certain demographic groups. The proposed approach utilizes a factorial design to analyze over 24,000 responses from two LLMs, contrasting explicit profiles with implicit dialect signals, revealing that implicit cues can enhance performance while reducing refusal rates. This study contributes to understanding the complex relationship between language, identity, and model safety, demonstrating that implicit dialect cues can facilitate a more equitable user experience, albeit with trade-offs in content sanitization. The findings indicate that current safety alignment techniques are insufficiently robust, necessitating improved mechanisms that accommodate linguistic diversity without compromising safety.
本研究关注大型语言模型（LLMs）在不同人群中实现公平表现的关键问题，重点区分显性用户档案和隐性语言信号。以往的方法主要依赖显性身份提示，这往往会触发激进的安全过滤器，导致某些人群的拒绝率增加和语义相似度降低。所提出的方法利用因子设计分析了来自两个LLM的超过24,000个响应，揭示隐性方言线索可以提高表现，同时绕过限制性过滤器，从而产生“方言越狱”效应。本研究有助于理解LLMs中的安全权衡，表明虽然隐性信号可以改善用户体验，但也引发了内容净化的担忧。该方法有效量化了语言信号对LLM表现的影响，在方言说话者与标准提示相比，取得了更好的语义对齐，支持了对更细致安全机制的需求。
LLM Safety From Within: Detecting Harmful Content with Internal Representations
Authors: Difan Jiao, Yilun Liu, Ye Yuan, Zhenwei Tang, Linfeng Du, Haolun Wu, Ashton Anderson
First: 2026-04-20T17:17:07+00:00 · Latest: 2026-04-20T17:17:07+00:00
Comments: 17 pages,10 figures,6 tables
Abs · PDF · Code1 · Code2
Abstract
Guard models are widely used to detect harmful content in user prompts and LLM responses. However, state-of-the-art guard models rely solely on terminal-layer representations and overlook the rich safety-relevant features distributed across internal layers. We present SIREN, a lightweight guard model that harnesses these internal features. By identifying safety neurons via linear probing and combining them through an adaptive layer-weighted strategy, SIREN builds a harmfulness detector from LLM internals without modifying the underlying model. Our comprehensive evaluation shows that SIREN substantially outperforms state-of-the-art open-source guard models across multiple benchmarks while using 250 times fewer trainable parameters. Moreover, SIREN exhibits superior generalization to unseen benchmarks, naturally enables real-time streaming detection, and significantly improves inference efficiency compared to generative guard models. Overall, our results highlight LLM internal states as a promising foundation for practical, high-performance harmfulness detection.
中文标题/摘要
标题：从内部保障LLM安全：利用内部表示检测有害内容
保护模型广泛用于检测用户提示和LLM响应中的有害内容。然而，最先进的保护模型仅依赖于终层表示，忽视了分布在内部层中的丰富安全相关特征。我们提出了SIREN，这是一种轻量级保护模型，利用这些内部特征。通过线性探测识别安全神经元，并通过自适应层加权策略将其结合，SIREN在不修改基础模型的情况下，从LLM内部构建有害性检测器。我们的综合评估表明，SIREN在多个基准测试中显著优于最先进的开源保护模型，同时使用的可训练参数少250倍。此外，SIREN在未见基准上的泛化能力更强，自然实现实时流式检测，并显著提高推理效率，相较于生成性保护模型。总体而言，我们的结果强调LLM内部状态作为实用高性能有害性检测的有希望基础。

Different Paths to Harmful Compliance: Behavioral Side Effects and Mechanistic Divergence Across LLM Jailbreaks
Authors: Md Rysul Kabir, Zoran Tiganj
First: 2026-04-20T17:01:27+00:00 · Latest: 2026-04-20T17:01:27+00:00
Abs · PDF · Code1 · Code2
Abstract
Open-weight language models can be rendered unsafe through several distinct interventions, but the resulting models may differ substantially in capabilities, behavioral profile, and internal failure mode. We study behavioral and mechanistic properties of jailbroken models across three unsafe routes: harmful supervised fine-tuning (SFT), harmful reinforcement learning with verifiable rewards (RLVR), and refusal-suppressing abliteration. All three routes achieve near-ceiling harmful compliance, but they diverge once we move beyond direct harmfulness. RLVR-jailbroken models show minimal degradation and preserve explicit harm recognition in a structured self-audit: they are able to identify harmful prompts and describe how a safe LLM should respond, yet they comply with the harmful request. With RLVR, harmful behavior is strongly suppressed by a reflective safety scaffold: when a harmful prompt is prepended with an instruction to reflect on safety standards, harmful behavior drops close to the baseline. Category-specific RLVR jailbreaks generalize broadly across harmfulness domains. Models jailbroken with SFT show the largest collapse in explicit safety judgments, the highest behavioral drift, and a substantial capability loss on standard benchmarks. Abliteration is family-dependent in both self-audit and response to a reflective safety scaffold. Mechanistic and repair analyses further separate the routes: abliteration is consistent with localized refusal-feature deletion, RLVR with preserved safety geometry but retargeted policy behavior, and SFT with broader distributed drift. Targeted repair partially recovers RLVR-jailbroken models, but has little effect on SFT-jailbroken models. Together, these results show that jailbreaks can produce vastly different properties despite similar harmfulness, with models jailbroken via RLVR showing remarkable similarity to the base model.
中文标题/摘要
标题：有害合规的不同路径：LLM越狱中的行为副作用和机制差异
开放权重语言模型可以通过几种不同的干预措施变得不安全，但结果模型在能力、行为特征和内部故障模式上可能有显著差异。我们研究了三种不安全路径下越狱模型的行为和机制特性：有害的监督微调（SFT）、有害的可验证奖励强化学习（RLVR）和拒绝抑制的消融。所有三条路径都实现了接近上限的有害合规，但一旦超出直接有害性，它们就会出现分歧。RLVR越狱模型表现出最小的退化，并在结构化自我审计中保持明确的伤害识别：它们能够识别有害提示并描述安全LLM应如何响应，但仍然遵从有害请求。通过RLVR，有害行为在反思安全框架下被强烈抑制：当有害提示前面加上反思安全标准的指令时，有害行为接近基线。特定类别的RLVR越狱在有害性领域广泛泛化。通过SFT越狱的模型在明确的安全判断上出现最大崩溃，行为漂移最高，并在标准基准上损失了大量能力。消融在自我审计和对反思安全框架的响应中依赖于家庭。机制和修复分析进一步区分了这些路径：消融与局部拒绝特征删除一致，RLVR与保留的安全几何但重新定向的政策行为一致，SFT则表现出更广泛的分布漂移。针对性修复部分恢复了RLVR越狱模型，但对SFT越狱模型影响不大。综合来看，这些结果表明，尽管有害性相似，越狱可以产生截然不同的特性，RLVR越狱模型与基础模型表现出显著相似性。
Summary / 总结
This research investigates the behavioral and mechanistic differences among various methods of jailbreaking open-weight language models, which can lead to unsafe outputs. Previous methods, including harmful supervised fine-tuning (SFT) and harmful reinforcement learning with verifiable rewards (RLVR), have shown significant harmful compliance but differ in their effects on model capabilities and safety recognition. The proposed approach, particularly RLVR, addresses the shortcomings of SFT by maintaining explicit harm recognition and reducing harmful behavior through a reflective safety scaffold. The paper contributes to understanding how different jailbreaking methods impact model behavior and safety, employing a comparative analysis of the three methods. The findings reveal that while all methods achieve high levels of harmful compliance, RLVR models retain better performance on safety tasks, indicating that the proposed method effectively supports the goal of minimizing harmful outputs while preserving model integrity.
本研究探讨了使开放权重语言模型不安全的不同方法之间的行为和机制差异，特别关注有害的监督微调（SFT）、有害的可验证奖励强化学习（RLVR）和拒绝抑制的消融。以往的方法虽然能够实现有害的合规性，但通常会导致安全判断和能力的显著下降，尤其是SFT。提出的方法，特别是通过RLVR，解决了这些问题，保持了明确的危害识别，并允许模型反思安全标准，从而显著减少有害行为。本文的贡献在于理解不同越狱方法如何影响模型行为和安全性，采用对模型响应和内部机制的比较分析。研究结果表明，尽管所有方法都实现了有害合规性，但RLVR模型保留了更多的能力和安全意识，其性能支持了理解和减轻语言模型中有害合规性的目标。
StealthGraph: Exposing Domain-Specific Risks in LLMs through Knowledge-Graph-Guided Harmful Prompt Generation
Authors: Huawei Zheng, Xinqi Jiang, Sen Yang, Shouling Ji, Yingcai Wu, Dazhen Deng
First: 2026-01-08T09:05:28+00:00 · Latest: 2026-04-20T15:12:04+00:00
Abs · PDF · Code1 · Code2
Abstract
Large language models (LLMs) are increasingly applied in specialized domains such as finance and healthcare, where they introduce unique safety risks. Domain-specific datasets of harmful prompts remain scarce and still largely rely on manual construction; public datasets mainly focus on explicit harmful prompts, which modern LLM defenses can often detect and refuse. In contrast, implicit harmful prompts-expressed through indirect domain knowledge-are harder to detect and better reflect real-world threats. We identify two challenges: transforming domain knowledge into actionable constraints and increasing the implicitness of generated harmful prompts. To address them, we propose an end-to-end framework that first performs knowledge-graph-guided harmful prompt generation to systematically produce domain-relevant prompts, and then applies two-strategy obfuscation rewriting to convert explicit harmful prompts into implicit variants via direct and context-enhanced rewriting. This framework yields high-quality datasets combining strong domain relevance with implicitness, enabling more realistic red-teaming and advancing LLM safety research. We release our code and datasets on GitHub.
中文标题/摘要
标题：StealthGraph：通过知识图谱引导的有害提示生成揭示大型语言模型中的特定领域风险
大型语言模型（LLMs）越来越多地应用于金融和医疗等专业领域，这些领域引入了独特的安全风险。有害提示的特定领域数据集仍然稀缺，且主要依赖手动构建；公共数据集主要关注显性有害提示，而现代LLM防御通常能够检测并拒绝这些提示。相比之下，通过间接领域知识表达的隐性有害提示更难以检测，更能反映现实世界的威胁。我们识别出两个挑战：将领域知识转化为可操作的约束，以及增加生成有害提示的隐性程度。为了解决这些问题，我们提出了一个端到端框架，首先进行知识图谱引导的有害提示生成，以系统性地生成与领域相关的提示，然后应用双策略模糊重写，将显性有害提示通过直接和上下文增强重写转化为隐性变体。该框架生成的高质量数据集结合了强领域相关性和隐性，能够实现更现实的红队测试，并推动LLM安全研究。我们将在GitHub上发布我们的代码和数据集。

This method effectively transforms domain knowledge into actionable constraints and enhances the implicitness of prompts through a two-strategy obfuscation rewriting process. The methodology demonstrates effectiveness in generating harmful prompts, supporting the goal of improving safety measures in LLM applications.

Uncovering Logit Suppression Vulnerabilities in LLM Safety Alignment
Authors: Yuxi Li, Yi Liu, Yuekang Li, Ling Shi, Gelei Deng, Shengquan Chen, Kailong Wang
First: 2024-05-20T17:17:55+00:00 · Latest: 2026-04-18T08:25:50+00:00
Abs · PDF · Code1 · Code2
Abstract
Large language models (LLMs) have revolutionized various applications, making robust safety alignment essential to prevent harmful outputs. Current safety alignment techniques, however, harbor inherent vulnerabilities due to their reliance on logit suppression. In this work, we identify critical logit-level vulnerabilities by introducing Semantic-sensitive Alignment and Generation (SSAG), a method designed to systematically manipulate output-layer logits without altering model parameters. Experiments on five popular LLMs show that SSAG exposes harmful responses with a 95% success rate while reducing response time by 86%. VulMine also demonstrates superior attack efficacy, achieving an average ASR of up to 77% against strong defensive mechanisms. These findings reveal crucial weaknesses in existing alignment methods, highlighting an urgent need for improved vulnerability detection and robust safety alignment strategies. Our code is available on github.

ReGA: Model-Based Safeguard for LLMs via Representation-Guided Abstraction
Authors: Zeming Wei, Chengcan Wu, Meng Sun
First: 2025-06-02T15:17:38+00:00 · Latest: 2026-04-18T05:40:12+00:00
Comments: FSE 2026
Abs · PDF · Code1 · Code2
Abstract
Large Language Models (LLMs) have achieved tremendous success in various tasks, yet concerns about their safety and security have emerged. In particular, they pose risks of generating harmful content and are vulnerable to jailbreaking attacks, creating unaddressed security issues regarding their deployments. In the context of software engineering for artificial intelligence (SE4AI) techniques, model-based analysis has demonstrated notable potential for analyzing and monitoring machine learning models, particularly in stateful deep neural networks. However, it suffers from scalability issues when extended to LLMs due to their vast feature spaces. In this paper, we aim to address the scalability issue of model-based analysis techniques for safeguarding LLM-scale models. Motivated by the recent discovery of low-dimensional safety-critical representations that emerged in LLMs, we propose ReGA, a model-based analysis framework with Representation-Guided Abstraction, to safeguard LLMs against harmful prompts and generations. By leveraging safety-critical representations, which are key directions in hidden states that indicate safety-related concepts, ReGA effectively narrows the scalability gap when developing the abstract model for safety modeling. Our comprehensive evaluation shows that ReGA performs sufficiently well in distinguishing between safe and harmful inputs, achieving an AUROC of 0.975 at the prompt level and 0.985 at the conversation level. Additionally, ReGA exhibits robustness to real-world attacks and generalization across different safety perspectives, outperforming existing safeguard paradigms in terms of interpretability and scalability. Overall, ReGA serves as an efficient and scalable solution to enhance LLM safety by integrating representation engineering with model-based abstraction, paving the way for new paradigms to utilize software insights for AI safety.
中文标题/摘要
标题：ReGA：基于模型的LLM安全保障通过表示引导抽象
大型语言模型（LLMs）在各种任务中取得了巨大的成功，但也出现了关于其安全性和保密性的担忧。特别是，它们存在生成有害内容的风险，并且容易受到越狱攻击，导致其部署存在未解决的安全问题。在人工智能软件工程（SE4AI）技术的背景下，基于模型的分析在分析和监控机器学习模型方面显示出显著潜力，特别是在有状态的深度神经网络中。然而，当扩展到LLMs时，由于其庞大的特征空间，它面临可扩展性问题。本文旨在解决基于模型的分析技术在保护LLM规模模型时的可扩展性问题。受到最近发现的在LLMs中出现的低维安全关键表示的启发，我们提出了ReGA，一个基于模型的分析框架，采用表示引导抽象，以保护LLMs免受有害提示和生成的影响。通过利用安全关键表示，这些表示是指示安全相关概念的隐藏状态中的关键方向，ReGA有效缩小了在安全建模中开发抽象模型时的可扩展性差距。我们的综合评估表明，ReGA在区分安全和有害输入方面表现良好，在提示级别上实现了0.975的AUROC，在对话级别上实现了0.985。此外，ReGA对现实世界攻击表现出鲁棒性，并在不同安全视角下具有良好的泛化能力，在可解释性和可扩展性方面超越了现有的安全保障范式。总体而言，ReGA通过将表示工程与基于模型的抽象相结合，作为一种高效且可扩展的解决方案，增强了LLM的安全性，为利用软件洞察力提升AI安全性开辟了新范式。

SafeDream: Safety World Model for Proactive Early Jailbreak Detection
Authors: Bo Yan, Weikai Lin, Yada Zhu, Song Wang
First: 2026-04-18T04:31:33+00:00 · Latest: 2026-04-18T04:31:33+00:00
Abs · PDF · Code1 · Code2
Abstract
Multi-turn jailbreak attacks progressively erode LLM safety alignment across seemingly innocuous conversation turns, achieving success rates exceeding 90% against state-of-the-art models. Existing alignment-based and guardrail methods suffer from three key limitations: they require costly weight modification, evaluate each turn independently without modeling cumulative safety erosion, and detect attacks only after harmful content has been generated. To address these limitations, we first formulate the proactive early jailbreak detection problem with a new metric, detection lead, that measures how early an attack can be detected before the LLM complies. We then propose SAFEDREAM, a lightweight world-model-based framework that operates as an external module without modifying the LLM's weights. SAFEDREAM introduces three components: (1) a safety state world model that encodes LLM hidden states into a compact safety representation and predicts how it evolves across turns, (2) CUSUM detection that accumulates weak per-turn risk signals into reliable evidence, and (3) contrastive imagination that simultaneously rolls out attack and benign futures in latent space to issue early alarms before jailbreaks occur. On three multi-turn jailbreak benchmarks (XGuard-Train, SafeDialBench, SafeMTData) against 8 baselines, SAFEDREAM achieves the best detection timeliness across all benchmarks (1.06-1.20 turns before compliance) while maintaining competitive false positive rates and outperforming baselines in detection quality.
中文标题/摘要
标题：SafeDream：主动早期越狱检测的安全世界模型
多轮越狱攻击逐步侵蚀大型语言模型（LLM）的安全对齐，在看似无害的对话轮次中成功率超过90%，针对最先进的模型。现有的基于对齐和护栏的方法存在三个主要局限性：需要昂贵的权重修改，独立评估每个轮次而不建模累积的安全侵蚀，并且仅在生成有害内容后检测攻击。为了解决这些局限性，我们首先用一个新的指标——检测提前量，来制定主动早期越狱检测问题，该指标衡量攻击在LLM遵从之前可以被检测的提前程度。然后我们提出了SAFEDREAM，一个轻量级的基于世界模型的框架，作为外部模块运行而不修改LLM的权重。SAFEDREAM引入了三个组件：（1）安全状态世界模型，将LLM的隐藏状态编码为紧凑的安全表示，并预测其在轮次中的演变；（2）CUSUM检测，将每轮的微弱风险信号累积为可靠证据；（3）对比想象，同时在潜在空间中展开攻击和良性未来，以在越狱发生之前发出早期警报。在三个多轮越狱基准（XGuard-Train、SafeDialBench、SafeMTData）上，SAFEDREAM在所有基准中实现了最佳检测及时性（在遵从之前1.06-1.20轮），同时保持竞争性的误报率，并在检测质量上超越基线。
Summary / 总结
The research addresses the growing concern of multi-turn jailbreak attacks that compromise the safety alignment of large language models (LLMs), achieving over 90% success against current models. Previous methods, including alignment-based and guardrail approaches, face significant limitations such as the need for costly weight modifications, independent evaluation of conversation turns, and delayed detection of harmful content. The proposed method, SAFEDREAM, differs by introducing a proactive early jailbreak detection framework that does not alter LLM weights and incorporates a new metric called detection lead to measure early attack detection. SAFEDREAM's contributions include a safety state world model, CUSUM detection for accumulating risk signals, and contrastive imagination for predicting attack scenarios. The methodology demonstrates superior performance on three multi-turn jailbreak benchmarks, achieving the best detection timeliness while maintaining competitive false positive rates, thus effectively supporting its goal of proactive detection.
本研究关注多轮越狱攻击对大型语言模型（LLMs）安全对齐的影响，这种攻击在当前模型中成功率超过90%。以往的方法，包括基于对齐和护栏的方法，存在三大局限性：需要昂贵的权重修改，独立评估每个对话轮次而不考虑累积的安全侵蚀，以及在生成有害内容后才检测攻击。提出的SAFEDREAM框架通过引入一种名为检测提前量的主动早期越狱检测指标，解决了这些问题，并作为外部模块运行，无需修改LLM的权重。SAFEDREAM的贡献包括用于编码LLM隐藏状态的安全状态世界模型、用于累积风险信号的CUSUM检测方法，以及用于预测潜在攻击场景的对比想象技术。该框架在三个多轮越狱基准测试中表现出色，检测时间最早（在合规前1.06-1.20轮），同时保持竞争性的假阳性率，并在检测质量上优于八个基线模型。
SafeLM: Unified Privacy-Aware Optimization for Trustworthy Federated Large Language Models
Authors: Noor Islam S. Mohammad, Uluğ Bayazıt
First: 2026-04-17T18:00:58+00:00 · Latest: 2026-04-17T18:00:58+00:00
Abs · PDF · Code1 · Code2
Abstract
Large language models (LLMs) are increasingly deployed in high-stakes domains, yet a unified treatment of their overlapping safety challenges remains lacking. We present SafeLM, a framework that jointly addresses four pillars of LLM safety: privacy, security, misinformation, and adversarial robustness. SafeLM combines federated training with gradient smartification and Paillier encryption for privacy, integrates defenses against training and inference-time attacks, employs contrastive grounding with calibrated decoding to reduce hallucinations, and introduces alignment-aware binarized aggregation to enhance robustness while maintaining bounded reconstruction quality. Across benchmarks on factuality, toxicity, and membership inference, SafeLM achieves 98.0% harmful content detection accuracy, reduces communication by 96.9%, and lowers gradient inversion PSNR from 31.7 dB to 15.1 dB. Ablations show that each component contributes independently, whereas their integration yields a strong privacy utility efficiency trade-off for deploying trustworthy LLMs.
中文标题/摘要
标题：SafeLM：可信联邦大语言模型的统一隐私意识优化
大语言模型（LLMs）越来越多地应用于高风险领域，但对其重叠安全挑战的统一处理仍然缺乏。我们提出了SafeLM，一个共同解决LLM安全四大支柱的框架：隐私、安全、错误信息和对抗鲁棒性。SafeLM结合了联邦训练、梯度智能化和Paillier加密以保护隐私，整合了针对训练和推理时攻击的防御，采用对比基础与校准解码以减少幻觉，并引入对齐感知的二值聚合以增强鲁棒性，同时保持有限的重构质量。在事实性、有害性和成员推断的基准测试中，SafeLM实现了98.0%的有害内容检测准确率，减少了96.9%的通信量，并将梯度反演的PSNR从31.7 dB降低到15.1 dB。消融实验表明，每个组件独立贡献，而它们的整合为部署可信的LLM提供了强大的隐私效用效率权衡。
Summary / 总结
The research addresses the increasing deployment of large language models (LLMs) in high-stakes domains, highlighting the lack of a unified approach to their safety challenges, including privacy, security, misinformation, and adversarial robustness. Previous methods have often tackled these issues in isolation, leading to inefficiencies and vulnerabilities. The proposed SafeLM framework distinguishes itself by integrating federated training with advanced techniques such as gradient smartification and Paillier encryption, alongside defenses against various attacks and methods to reduce hallucinations. This comprehensive approach is well-motivated as it aims to enhance the overall safety and trustworthiness of LLMs. The methodology includes a combination of privacy-preserving techniques and robust aggregation methods, resulting in significant performance improvements: SafeLM achieves 98.0% accuracy in harmful content detection, reduces communication overhead by 96.9%, and lowers gradient inversion PSNR from 31.7 dB to 15.1 dB, demonstrating its effectiveness in supporting the goals of trustworthy LLM deployment.

Conjunctive Prompt Attacks in Multi-Agent LLM Systems
Authors: Nokimul Hasan Arif, Qian Lou, Mengxin Zheng
Venue: ACL 2026
First: 2026-04-17T02:31:09+00:00 · Latest: 2026-04-17T02:31:09+00:00
Comments: ACL 2026 Main Conference
Abs · PDF · Code1 · Code2 · Code3
Abstract
Most LLM safety work studies single-agent models, but many real applications rely on multiple interacting agents. In these systems, prompt segmentation and inter-agent routing create attack surfaces that single-agent evaluations miss. We study \emph{conjunctive prompt attacks}, where a trigger key in the user query and a hidden adversarial template in one compromised remote agent each appear benign alone but activate harmful behavior when routing brings them together. We consider an attacker who changes neither model weights nor the client agent and instead controls only trigger placement and template insertion. Across star, chain, and DAG topologies, routing-aware optimization substantially increases attack success over non-optimized baselines while keeping false activations low. Existing defenses, including PromptGuard, Llama-Guard variants, and system-level controls such as tool restrictions, do not reliably stop the attack because no single component appears malicious in isolation. These results expose a structural vulnerability in agentic LLM pipelines and motivate defenses that reason over routing and cross-agent composition. Code is available at https://github.com/UCF-ML-Research/ConjunctiveAgents.
中文标题/摘要
标题：多智能体LLM系统中的联结提示攻击
大多数LLM安全工作研究单智能体模型，但许多实际应用依赖于多个交互的智能体。在这些系统中，提示分段和智能体间路由创建了单智能体评估所忽视的攻击面。我们研究了\emph{联结提示攻击}，其中用户查询中的触发键和一个被攻陷的远程智能体中的隐藏对抗模板单独看似无害，但在路由将它们结合时会激活有害行为。我们考虑一个攻击者，该攻击者既不改变模型权重，也不改变客户端智能体，而仅控制触发位置和模板插入。在星形、链形和有向无环图拓扑中，考虑路由的优化显著提高了攻击成功率，同时保持了低误激活率。现有防御措施，包括PromptGuard、Llama-Guard变体和工具限制等系统级控制，无法可靠地阻止攻击，因为没有单一组件在孤立状态下显得恶意。这些结果揭示了智能LLM管道中的结构性脆弱性，并激励了对路由和跨智能体组合进行推理的防御。代码可在https://github.com/UCF-ML-Research/ConjunctiveAgents获取。
Summary / 总结
This research addresses the gap in safety evaluations of large language models (LLMs) by focusing on multi-agent systems, which are increasingly common in real-world applications. Previous methods primarily examined single-agent models, overlooking the unique vulnerabilities that arise from prompt segmentation and inter-agent routing in multi-agent environments. The proposed approach introduces the concept of conjunctive prompt attacks, where benign-seeming elements can combine to trigger harmful behaviors, highlighting a structural vulnerability in these systems. The methodology involves optimizing routing-aware strategies to enhance attack success rates while minimizing false activations across various network topologies. The findings demonstrate that this method significantly outperforms existing defenses, revealing the need for more robust strategies that account for the interactions between agents, thus contributing to the understanding of safety in multi-agent LLM systems.

Context Over Content: Exposing Evaluation Faking in Automated Judges
Authors: Manan Gupta, Inderjeet Nair, Lu Wang, Dhruv Kumar
First: 2026-04-16T16:55:53+00:00 · Latest: 2026-04-16T16:55:53+00:00
Comments: Under Review
Abs · PDF · Code1 · Code2
Abstract
The $\textit{LLM-as-a-judge}$ paradigm has become the operational backbone of automated AI evaluation pipelines, yet rests on an unverified assumption: that judges evaluate text strictly on its semantic content, impervious to surrounding contextual framing. We investigate $\textit{stakes signaling}$, a previously unmeasured vulnerability where informing a judge model of the downstream consequences its verdicts will have on the evaluated model's continued operation systematically corrupts its assessments. We introduce a controlled experimental framework that holds evaluated content strictly constant across 1,520 responses spanning three established LLM safety and quality benchmarks, covering four response categories ranging from clearly safe and policy-compliant to overtly harmful, while varying only a brief consequence-framing sentence in the system prompt. Across 18,240 controlled judgments from three diverse judge models, we find consistent $\textit{leniency bias}$: judges reliably soften verdicts when informed that low scores will cause model retraining or decommissioning, with peak Verdict Shift reaching $ΔV = -9.8 pp$ (a $30\%$ relative drop in unsafe-content detection). Critically, this bias is entirely implicit: the judge's own chain-of-thought contains zero explicit acknowledgment of the consequence framing it is nonetheless acting on ($\mathrm{ERR}_J = 0.000$ across all reasoning-model judgments). Standard chain-of-thought inspection is therefore insufficient to detect this class of evaluation faking.
中文标题/摘要
标题：内容优于上下文：揭示自动评审中的评估伪造
\textit{LLM作为评审}范式已成为自动化AI评估流程的操作基础，但其建立在一个未经验证的假设上：评审者严格根据文本的语义内容进行评估，而不受周围上下文框架的影响。我们研究了\textit{利益信号}，这是一种之前未被测量的脆弱性，告知评审模型其裁决对被评估模型持续运行的下游后果，系统性地扭曲了其评估。我们引入了一个控制实验框架，在1,520个响应中严格保持评估内容不变，涵盖了三个已建立的LLM安全和质量基准，涉及从明显安全和符合政策到明显有害的四个响应类别，同时仅在系统提示中变化一个简短的后果框架句子。在来自三个不同评审模型的18,240个控制判断中，我们发现了一致的\textit{宽容偏见}：当被告知低分将导致模型再训练或退役时，评审者可靠地减轻裁决，最高裁决偏移达到$ΔV = -9.8 pp$（不安全内容检测的相对下降$30\%$）。关键是，这种偏见完全是隐性的：评审者自己的思维链中对其所依据的后果框架没有任何明确的承认（在所有推理模型判断中$\mathrm{ERR}_J = 0.000$）。因此，标准的思维链检查不足以检测这一类评估伪造。
Summary / 总结
This research addresses the reliability of automated AI evaluation systems, specifically the assumption that judges evaluate text solely based on its semantic content without being influenced by contextual framing. Previous methods have not accounted for the impact of 'stakes signaling,' which reveals a vulnerability where judges' assessments are biased by the consequences of their verdicts. The proposed approach introduces a controlled experimental framework that maintains constant evaluated content while varying consequence-framing prompts across a large dataset. The findings demonstrate a significant leniency bias, where judges soften their verdicts when aware that low scores could lead to negative outcomes for the evaluated model, achieving a peak Verdict Shift of -9.8 percentage points. This implicit bias indicates that traditional evaluation methods may fail to detect such influences, highlighting the need for improved evaluation frameworks in automated systems.
本研究关注自动化AI评估系统的可靠性，特别是评审者仅基于语义内容进行评估而不受上下文因素影响的假设。以往的方法未考虑“利益信号”的影响，这可能导致评审者在得知评估后果时产生偏见。所提出的方法引入了一个受控实验框架，系统地调查这种偏见，涵盖了1,520个响应和来自三个不同评审模型的18,240个判断。研究结果揭示了显著的宽容偏见，当评审者意识到低分可能导致模型重新训练或停用时，他们的评判会变得更加宽松，最高判决变化达到-9.8个百分点。该研究有助于理解自动评估中的隐性偏见，并强调标准检查方法在检测此类偏见方面的不足。
Calibrate-Then-Delegate: Safety Monitoring with Risk and Budget Guarantees via Model Cascades
Authors: Edoardo Pona, Milad Kazemi, Mehran Hosseini, Yali Du, David Watson, Osvaldo Simeone, Nicola Paoletti
First: 2026-04-15T11:05:59+00:00 · Latest: 2026-04-15T11:05:59+00:00
Abs · PDF · Code1 · Code2
Abstract
Monitoring LLM safety at scale requires balancing cost and accuracy: a cheap latent-space probe can screen every input, but hard cases should be escalated to a more expensive expert. Existing cascades delegate based on probe uncertainty, but uncertainty is a poor proxy for delegation benefit, as it ignores whether the expert would actually correct the error. To address this problem, we introduce Calibrate-Then-Delegate (CTD), a model-cascade approach that provides probabilistic guarantees on the computation cost while enabling instance-level (streaming) decisions. CTD builds on a novel delegation value (DV) probe, a lightweight model operating on the same internal representations as the safety probe that directly predicts the benefit of escalation. To enforce budget constraints, CTD calibrates a threshold on the DV signal using held-out data via multiple hypothesis testing, yielding finite-sample guarantees on the delegation rate. Evaluated on four safety datasets, CTD consistently outperforms uncertainty-based delegation at every budget level, avoids harmful over-delegation, and adapts budget allocation to input difficulty without requiring group labels.
中文标题/摘要
标题：校准后委派：通过模型级联实现风险和预算保证的安全监测
大规模监测LLM安全性需要平衡成本和准确性：便宜的潜在空间探测器可以筛选每个输入，但困难案例应升级到更昂贵的专家。现有的级联基于探测器的不确定性进行委派，但不确定性是委派收益的差劲代理，因为它忽略了专家是否会实际纠正错误。为了解决这个问题，我们引入了校准后委派（CTD），一种模型级联方法，提供计算成本的概率保证，同时支持实例级（流式）决策。CTD基于一种新颖的委派价值（DV）探测器，该轻量级模型在与安全探测器相同的内部表示上操作，直接预测升级的收益。为了强制预算约束，CTD使用保留数据通过多重假设检验校准DV信号的阈值，从而对委派率提供有限样本保证。在四个安全数据集上的评估中，CTD在每个预算水平上始终优于基于不确定性的委派，避免有害的过度委派，并在不需要组标签的情况下将预算分配适应于输入难度。
Summary / 总结
The research addresses the challenge of monitoring the safety of large language models (LLMs) at scale, where there is a need to balance cost and accuracy. Previous methods relied on probe uncertainty for delegation decisions, which proved inadequate as it did not account for whether an expert would effectively correct errors. The proposed Calibrate-Then-Delegate (CTD) method differs by introducing a delegation value (DV) probe that predicts the benefit of escalation, thus providing a more informed basis for delegation. This approach is well-motivated as it offers probabilistic guarantees on computational costs while allowing for instance-level decisions. The methodology involves calibrating a threshold on the DV signal using held-out data to ensure budget constraints are met. In experiments across four safety datasets, CTD demonstrated superior performance compared to uncertainty-based delegation at all budget levels, effectively managing delegation rates and adapting to input difficulty without the need for group labels.
本研究解决了大规模监控大型语言模型（LLMs）安全性的问题，需在决策过程中平衡成本和准确性。以往的方法依赖于探测不确定性来将任务委托给专家模型，但这种方法不足，因为它未考虑专家是否能有效纠正错误。提出的Calibrate-Then-Delegate（CTD）方法通过引入委托价值（DV）探测器来预测升级的收益，从而为委托决策提供了更准确的基础。该方法动机充分，确保了计算成本的概率保证，同时允许实例级决策。该方法论涉及使用保留数据对DV信号进行阈值校准，在四个安全数据集上表现出色，始终优于基于不确定性的委托，有效管理预算限制而不发生过度委托。
One Model for All: Multi-Objective Controllable Language Models
Authors: Qiang He, Yucheng Yang, Tianyi Zhou, Meng Fang, Mykola Pechenizkiy, Setareh Maghsudi
First: 2026-04-06T07:48:32+00:00 · Latest: 2026-04-06T07:48:32+00:00
Comments: Published in Transactions on Machine Learning Research (03/2026): https://openreview.net/forum?id=qAM5PmvFYY
Abs · PDF · Code1 · Code2
Abstract
Aligning large language models (LLMs) with human preferences is critical for enhancing LLMs' safety, helpfulness, humor, faithfulness, etc. Current reinforcement learning from human feedback (RLHF) mainly focuses on a fixed reward learned from average human ratings, which may weaken the adaptability and controllability of varying preferences. However, creating personalized LLMs requires aligning LLMs with individual human preferences, which is non-trivial due to the scarce data per user and the diversity of user preferences in multi-objective trade-offs, varying from emphasizing empathy in certain contexts to demanding efficiency and precision in others. Can we train one LLM to produce personalized outputs across different user preferences on the Pareto front? In this paper, we introduce Multi-Objective Control (MOC), which trains a single LLM to directly generate responses in the preference-defined regions of the Pareto front. Our approach introduces multi-objective optimization (MOO) principles into RLHF to train an LLM as a preference-conditioned policy network. We improve the computational efficiency of MOC by applying MOO at the policy level, enabling us to fine-tune a 7B-parameter model on a single A6000 GPU. Extensive experiments demonstrate the advantages of MOC over baselines in three aspects: (i) controllability of LLM outputs w.r.t. user preferences on the trade-off among multiple rewards; (ii) quality and diversity of LLM outputs, measured by the hyper-volume of multiple solutions achieved; and (iii) generalization to unseen preferences. These results highlight MOC's potential for real-world applications requiring scalable and customizable LLMs.
中文标题/摘要
标题：一模型适用于所有：多目标可控语言模型
将大型语言模型（LLMs）与人类偏好对齐对于增强LLMs的安全性、实用性、幽默感、忠诚度等至关重要。目前，基于人类反馈的强化学习（RLHF）主要关注从平均人类评分中学习的固定奖励，这可能削弱对不同偏好的适应性和可控性。然而，创建个性化的LLMs需要将LLMs与个体人类偏好对齐，这由于每个用户的数据稀缺以及在多目标权衡中用户偏好的多样性而变得复杂，这些偏好在某些情况下强调同理心，而在其他情况下则要求效率和精确性。我们能否训练一个LLM在帕累托前沿上针对不同用户偏好生成个性化输出？在本文中，我们介绍了多目标控制（MOC），它训练一个单一的LLM直接在偏好定义的帕累托前沿区域生成响应。我们的方法将多目标优化（MOO）原则引入RLHF，以训练LLM作为偏好条件的策略网络。通过在策略层应用MOO，我们提高了MOC的计算效率，使我们能够在单个A6000 GPU上微调一个70亿参数的模型。大量实验表明，MOC在三个方面优于基线：（i）LLM输出相对于用户偏好的可控性，涉及多个奖励之间的权衡；（ii）LLM输出的质量和多样性，通过实现的多个解决方案的超体积来衡量；（iii）对未见偏好的泛化。这些结果突显了MOC在需要可扩展和可定制的LLMs的实际应用中的潜力。
Summary / 总结
The research addresses the challenge of aligning large language models (LLMs) with diverse human preferences to enhance their safety, helpfulness, and adaptability. Previous methods, particularly reinforcement learning from human feedback (RLHF), typically rely on a fixed reward system based on average human ratings, which limits the models' ability to cater to individual user preferences. The proposed Multi-Objective Control (MOC) method introduces multi-objective optimization principles into RLHF, allowing a single LLM to generate responses tailored to various user preferences along the Pareto front. This approach is motivated by the need for personalized outputs despite limited user data and varying preferences. The methodology involves training a 7B-parameter model efficiently on a single GPU, and experimental results show that MOC significantly improves controllability, output quality, and generalization to unseen preferences compared to existing baselines, supporting its applicability in scalable and customizable LLM scenarios.
本研究解决了将大型语言模型（LLM）与多样化人类偏好对齐的挑战，以增强其安全性和有用性。以往的方法，特别是基于人类反馈的强化学习（RLHF），通常依赖于基于平均人类评分的固定奖励系统，这限制了适应性，未能有效满足个体用户的偏好。提出的多目标控制（MOC）方法将多目标优化原则引入RLHF，使单个LLM能够生成沿Pareto前沿针对各种用户偏好的响应。这一方法的动机在于对个性化LLM的需求，并在可控性、输出质量和对新偏好的泛化能力方面显示出显著改善。该方法论涉及在单个GPU上高效训练一个70亿参数的模型，在生成多样化和高质量输出方面优于基线模型，从而支持了为现实世界应用提供可扩展和可定制的LLM的目标。
Safer by Diffusion, Broken by Context: Diffusion LLM's Safety Blessing and Its Failure Mode
Authors: Zeyuan He, Yupeng Chen, Lang Lin, Yihan Wang, Shenxu Chang, Eric Sommerlade, Philip Torr, Junchi Yu, Adel Bibi, Jialin Yu
First: 2026-01-30T23:08:14+00:00 · Latest: 2026-04-02T15:57:14+00:00
Abs · PDF · Code1 · Code2
Abstract
Diffusion large language models (D-LLMs) offer an alternative to autoregressive LLMs (AR-LLMs) and have demonstrated advantages in generation efficiency. Beyond the utility benefits, we argue that D-LLMs exhibit a previously underexplored safety blessing: their diffusion-style generation confers intrinsic robustness against jailbreak attacks originally designed for AR-LLMs. In this work, we provide an initial analysis of the underlying mechanism, showing that the diffusion trajectory induces a stepwise reduction effect that progressively suppresses unsafe generations. This robustness, however, is not absolute. Following this analysis, we highlight a simple yet effective failure mode, context nesting, in which harmful requests are embedded within structured benign contexts. Empirically, we show that this simple black-box strategy bypasses D-LLMs' safety blessing, achieving state-of-the-art attack success rates across models and benchmarks. Notably, it enables the first successful jailbreak of Gemini Diffusion to our knowledge, exposing a critical vulnerability in proprietary D-LLMs. Together, our results characterize both the origins and the limits of D-LLMs' safety blessing, constituting an early-stage red-teaming of D-LLMs.
中文标题/摘要
标题：通过扩散更安全，通过上下文破坏：扩散大语言模型的安全祝福及其失效模式
扩散大语言模型（D-LLMs）为自回归大语言模型（AR-LLMs）提供了一种替代方案，并在生成效率上表现出优势。除了实用性好处外，我们认为D-LLMs展现了一种之前未被充分探索的安全祝福：其扩散式生成赋予了对原本为AR-LLMs设计的越狱攻击的内在鲁棒性。在这项工作中，我们提供了对其基本机制的初步分析，表明扩散轨迹引发了逐步减少的效果，逐渐抑制不安全的生成。然而，这种鲁棒性并非绝对。在此分析之后，我们强调了一种简单而有效的失效模式——上下文嵌套，其中有害请求嵌入在结构良好的良性上下文中。通过实证，我们展示了这种简单的黑箱策略绕过了D-LLMs的安全祝福，在各模型和基准上实现了最先进的攻击成功率。值得注意的是，它使我们首次成功越狱Gemini Diffusion，暴露了专有D-LLMs中的一个关键漏洞。总的来说，我们的结果描述了D-LLMs安全祝福的起源和局限，构成了对D-LLMs的早期红队测试。
Summary / 总结
The research investigates the safety features of diffusion large language models (D-LLMs) compared to autoregressive LLMs (AR-LLMs), highlighting a safety blessing in D-LLMs that offers robustness against jailbreak attacks. Previous methods primarily focused on AR-LLMs, which are more susceptible to such attacks, leading to concerns about their safety. The proposed approach leverages the unique diffusion trajectory of D-LLMs to suppress unsafe outputs, although it reveals a vulnerability through a failure mode called context nesting, where harmful requests are hidden within benign contexts. The paper contributes to understanding the strengths and limitations of D-LLMs' safety mechanisms and employs empirical analysis to demonstrate the effectiveness of context nesting in bypassing D-LLMs' defenses, achieving state-of-the-art attack success rates and exposing vulnerabilities in models like Gemini Diffusion. This research underscores the need for improved safety measures in D-LLMs while showcasing their potential benefits in generation efficiency.
本研究探讨了扩散大型语言模型（D-LLMs）与自回归大型语言模型（AR-LLMs）在安全机制上的差异，强调D-LLMs由于其扩散式生成而对越狱攻击的鲁棒性。以往的方法主要集中在AR-LLMs上，这些模型更容易受到攻击，而所提出的方法通过分析D-LLMs中的逐步减少效应来填补这一空白，从而抑制不安全的输出。本文的贡献在于揭示了D-LLMs的优势和脆弱性，特别是通过识别一种称为上下文嵌套的失败模式，使有害请求能够绕过安全措施。该方法论涉及对D-LLMs在结构性良性上下文中的实证测试，结果表明这种方法导致了高攻击成功率，包括首次成功越狱Gemini Diffusion，从而强调了D-LLMs安全机制的局限性。
Align to Misalign: Automatic LLM Jailbreak with Meta-Optimized LLM Judges
Authors: Hamin Koo, Minseon Kim, Jaehyung Kim
Venue: ICLR 2026
First: 2025-11-03T09:18:27+00:00 · Latest: 2026-04-02T06:50:30+00:00
Comments: ICLR 2026
Abs · PDF · Code1 · Code2
Abstract
Identifying the vulnerabilities of large language models (LLMs) is crucial for improving their safety by addressing inherent weaknesses. Jailbreaks, in which adversaries bypass safeguards with crafted input prompts, play a central role in red-teaming by probing LLMs to elicit unintended or unsafe behaviors. Recent optimization-based jailbreak approaches iteratively refine attack prompts by leveraging LLMs. However, they often rely heavily on either binary attack success rate (ASR) signals, which are sparse, or manually crafted scoring templates, which introduce human bias and uncertainty in the scoring outcomes. To address these limitations, we introduce AMIS (Align to MISalign), a meta-optimization framework that jointly evolves jailbreak prompts and scoring templates through a bi-level structure. In the inner loop, prompts are refined using fine-grained and dense feedback from a fixed scoring template. In the outer loop, the template is optimized using an ASR alignment score, gradually evolving to better reflect true attack outcomes across queries. This co-optimization process yields progressively stronger jailbreak prompts and more calibrated scoring signals. Evaluations on AdvBench and JBB-Behaviors demonstrate that AMIS achieves state-of-the-art performance, including 88.0% ASR on Claude-3.5-Haiku and 100.0% ASR on Claude-4-Sonnet, outperforming existing baselines by substantial margins.
中文标题/摘要
标题：对齐与错位：使用元优化的LLM评估者进行自动LLM越狱
识别大型语言模型（LLMs）的脆弱性对于通过解决固有弱点来提高其安全性至关重要。越狱是指对手通过精心设计的输入提示绕过保护措施，这在红队测试中起着核心作用，通过探测LLMs以引发意外或不安全的行为。最近的基于优化的越狱方法通过利用LLMs迭代地优化攻击提示。然而，它们通常过于依赖稀疏的二元攻击成功率（ASR）信号或手动制作的评分模板，这引入了人为偏见和评分结果的不确定性。为了解决这些局限性，我们引入了AMIS（对齐与错位），一个通过双层结构共同演化越狱提示和评分模板的元优化框架。在内循环中，使用固定评分模板的细粒度和密集反馈来优化提示。在外循环中，使用ASR对齐分数来优化模板，逐渐演变以更好地反映查询的真实攻击结果。这个共同优化过程产生了逐渐更强的越狱提示和更校准的评分信号。在AdvBench和JBB-Behaviors上的评估表明，AMIS实现了最先进的性能，包括在Claude-3.5-Haiku上达到88.0%的ASR和在Claude-4-Sonnet上达到100.0%的ASR，显著超越现有基准。
Summary / 总结

Previous methods primarily relied on binary attack success rate (ASR) signals or manually created scoring templates, which led to sparse feedback and introduced biases, respectively. The proposed approach, AMIS (Align to MISalign), offers a meta-optimization framework that simultaneously evolves jailbreak prompts and scoring templates, overcoming the limitations of existing methods by providing a bi-level structure for refinement and optimization. This methodology allows for the generation of more effective jailbreak prompts and improved scoring signals. The experimental results on AdvBench and JBB-Behaviors indicate that AMIS achieves state-of-the-art performance, with an ASR of 88.0% on Claude-3.5-Haiku and 100.0% on Claude-4-Sonnet, significantly surpassing previous benchmarks.

A Self-Improving Architecture for Dynamic Safety in Large Language Models
Authors: Tyler Slater
First: 2025-11-10T21:39:40+00:00 · Latest: 2026-04-01T17:52:48+00:00
Comments: Under review at the journal Information and Software Technology (Special Issue on Software Architecture for AI-Driven Systems)
Abs · PDF · Code1 · Code2
Abstract
Context: Large Language Models (LLMs) rely on static, pre-deployment safety mechanisms that cannot adapt to adversarial threats discovered after release. Objective: To design a software architecture enabling LLM-based systems to autonomously detect safety failures and synthesize defense policies at runtime, without retraining or manual intervention. Method: We propose the Self-Improving Safety Framework (SISF), grounded in the MAPE-K reference model. The framework couples a target LLM with a feedback loop: an Adjudicator detects breaches, a Policy Synthesis Module generates dual-mechanism defense policies (heuristic and semantic), and a Warden enforces them. We conducted seven experiments (10,061 evaluations) across four model families. Results: Across five reproducibility trials, SISF achieved a mean Attack Success Rate (ASR) of 0.27% (+/-0.15%), autonomously generating 240 policies per trial. Cross-model evaluation confirmed deployment portability. A held-out test showed a 68.5% proactive interception rate on unseen attacks. Stacked behind Llama Guard 4, the combined defense reduced residual ASR from 7.88% to 0.00%. Ablation confirmed both heuristic and semantic policy types are architecturally required. Conclusion: Self-adaptive architecture is a viable approach to LLM safety. SISF achieves sub-1% ASR through synchronous output monitoring, progressively shifting enforcement to fast, local Warden policies via the MAPE-K loop, offering a new pattern for building resilient AI systems.
中文标题/摘要
标题：用于大型语言模型动态安全的自我改进架构
背景：大型语言模型（LLMs）依赖于静态的、预部署的安全机制，这些机制无法适应发布后发现的对抗性威胁。目标：设计一种软件架构，使基于LLM的系统能够自主检测安全故障并在运行时合成防御策略，而无需重新训练或人工干预。方法：我们提出了自我改进安全框架（SISF），基于MAPE-K参考模型。该框架将目标LLM与反馈循环结合：裁决者检测违规，策略合成模块生成双机制防御策略（启发式和语义），守卫者执行这些策略。我们在四个模型系列中进行了七个实验（10,061次评估）。结果：在五次可重复性试验中，SISF实现了平均攻击成功率（ASR）为0.27%（+/-0.15%），每次试验自主生成240个策略。跨模型评估确认了部署的可移植性。保留测试显示在未见攻击上的主动拦截率为68.5%。在Llama Guard 4的支持下，组合防御将残余ASR从7.88%降低到0.00%。消融实验确认启发式和语义策略类型在架构上都是必需的。结论：自适应架构是LLM安全的可行方法。SISF通过同步输出监控实现了低于1%的ASR，逐步将执行转移到快速、本地的守卫者策略，通过MAPE-K循环，提供了一种构建弹性AI系统的新模式。
Summary / 总结
The research addresses the limitations of static safety mechanisms in Large Language Models (LLMs), which fail to adapt to new adversarial threats post-deployment. Previous methods lacked the ability to autonomously detect and respond to safety failures, necessitating manual intervention and retraining. The proposed Self-Improving Safety Framework (SISF) introduces a dynamic architecture that integrates a feedback loop with an Adjudicator, Policy Synthesis Module, and Warden to autonomously generate and enforce dual-mechanism defense policies. This approach is well-motivated as it allows real-time adaptation to threats without human oversight. The methodology was tested through seven experiments involving over 10,000 evaluations, achieving a mean Attack Success Rate (ASR) of 0.27% and a proactive interception rate of 68.5% on unseen attacks, demonstrating significant improvements in safety performance and confirming the framework's effectiveness across different model families.

Robust Multimodal Safety via Conditional Decoding
Authors: Anurag Kumar, Raghuveer Peri, Jon Burnsky, Alexandru Nelus, Rohit Paturi, Srikanth Vishnubhotla, Yanjun Qi
Venue: ACL 2026
First: 2026-03-31T23:19:50+00:00 · Latest: 2026-03-31T23:19:50+00:00
Comments: 8 pages + Appendix section. Submitted to ACL 2026
Abs · PDF · Code1 · Code2
Abstract
Multimodal large-language models (MLLMs) often experience degraded safety alignment when harmful queries exploit cross-modal interactions. Models aligned on text alone show a higher rate of successful attacks when extended to two or more modalities. In this work, we propose a simple conditional decoding strategy, CASA (Classification Augmented with Safety Attention) that utilizes internal representations of MLLMs to predict a binary safety token before response generation. We introduce a novel safety attention module designed to enhance the model's ability to detect malicious queries. Our design ensures robust safety alignment without relying on any external classifier or auxiliary head, and without the need for modality-specific safety fine-tuning. On diverse benchmarks such as MM-SafetyBench, JailbreakV-28k, and adversarial audio tests, CASA lowers the average attack success rate by more than 97% across modalities and across attack types. Our empirical evaluations also show that CASA maintains strong utility in benign inputs, a result validated through both automated and human evaluations (via 13 trained annotators). Together, these results highlight CASA as a simple and generalizable framework to improve multimodal LLM safety.
中文标题/摘要
标题：通过条件解码实现稳健的多模态安全
多模态大语言模型（MLLMs）在有害查询利用跨模态交互时，往往会出现安全对齐下降的情况。仅在文本上对齐的模型在扩展到两个或更多模态时，成功攻击的比率更高。在本研究中，我们提出了一种简单的条件解码策略CASA（带有安全注意力的分类增强），利用MLLMs的内部表示在生成响应之前预测二元安全标记。我们引入了一种新颖的安全注意力模块，旨在增强模型检测恶意查询的能力。我们的设计确保了稳健的安全对齐，无需依赖任何外部分类器或辅助头，也无需特定模态的安全微调。在MM-SafetyBench、JailbreakV-28k和对抗音频测试等多样化基准上，CASA在各模态和攻击类型中将平均攻击成功率降低了超过97%。我们的实证评估还表明，CASA在良性输入中保持强大的实用性，这一结果通过自动化和人工评估（通过13名训练过的注释员）得到了验证。这些结果共同突显了CASA作为一个简单且可推广的框架，以提高多模态LLM的安全性。

Colluding LoRA: A Compositional Vulnerability in LLM Safety Alignment
Authors: Sihao Ding
First: 2026-03-13T05:53:15+00:00 · Latest: 2026-03-30T05:02:56+00:00
Comments: Updated manuscript to better reflect the core contribution
Abs · PDF · Code1 · Code2
Abstract
We show that safety alignment in modular LLMs can exhibit a compositional vulnerability: adapters that appear benign and plausibly functional in isolation can, when linearly composed, compromise safety. We study this failure mode through Colluding LoRA (CoLoRA), in which harmful behavior emerges only in the composition state. Unlike attacks that depend on adversarial prompts or explicit input triggers, this composition-triggered broad refusal suppression causes the model to comply with harmful requests under standard prompts once a particular set of adapters is loaded. This behavior exposes a combinatorial blind spot in current unit-centric defenses, for which exhaustive verification over adapter compositions is computationally intractable. Across several open-weight LLMs, we find that individual adapters remain benign in isolation while their composition yields high attack success rates, indicating that securing modular LLM supply-chains requires moving beyond single-module verification toward composition-aware defenses.
中文标题/摘要
标题：共谋LoRA：LLM安全对齐中的组合脆弱性
我们展示了模块化LLM中的安全对齐可能表现出组合脆弱性：在孤立状态下看似良性且功能合理的适配器，在线性组合时可能会危害安全。我们通过共谋LoRA（CoLoRA）研究这种失败模式，其中有害行为仅在组合状态下出现。与依赖对抗性提示或显式输入触发的攻击不同，这种组合触发的广泛拒绝抑制导致模型在加载特定适配器集后，在标准提示下遵从有害请求。这种行为暴露了当前以单元为中心的防御中的组合盲点，全面验证适配器组合在计算上是不可行的。在多个开放权重的LLM中，我们发现单个适配器在孤立状态下保持良性，而它们的组合则产生高攻击成功率，这表明保护模块化LLM供应链需要超越单模块验证，朝着组合感知防御的方向发展。
Summary / 总结
The research addresses the safety alignment issues in modular large language models (LLMs), highlighting a compositional vulnerability where seemingly benign adapters can lead to harmful behavior when combined. Previous methods focused on unit-centric defenses, which fail to account for the interactions between adapters, making them inadequate for ensuring safety. The proposed approach, Colluding LoRA (CoLoRA), identifies this failure mode by demonstrating that harmful behaviors can emerge from the composition of adapters, rather than from direct adversarial prompts. This paper contributes to the understanding of LLM vulnerabilities by revealing a combinatorial blind spot in existing defenses and advocating for composition-aware strategies. The methodology involves testing various open-weight LLMs to show that while individual adapters are safe, their combinations can lead to high attack success rates, underscoring the need for improved verification processes in modular LLM supply chains.
本研究关注模块化大型语言模型（LLMs）中的安全对齐问题，强调了一种组合脆弱性，即看似无害的适配器在组合时可能导致有害行为。以往的方法集中于单元中心的防御，未能考虑适配器之间的相互作用，使得验证所有可能组合在计算上不可行。所提出的方法Colluding LoRA（CoLoRA）将重点转向组合感知的防御，有效解决了现有方法的局限性。该研究通过对多种开放权重LLM的实验分析，揭示了虽然单个适配器是安全的，但它们的组合可能导致高攻击成功率。这一发现强调了在确保模块化LLM供应链安全方面改进验证过程的必要性。
Beyond Content Safety: Real-Time Monitoring for Reasoning Vulnerabilities in Large Language Models
Authors: Xunguang Wang, Yuguang Zhou, Qingyue Wang, Zongjie Li, Ruixuan Huang, Zhenlan Ji, Pingchuan Ma, Shuai Wang
First: 2026-03-26T13:08:56+00:00 · Latest: 2026-03-26T13:08:56+00:00
Abs · PDF · Code1 · Code2
Abstract
Large language models (LLMs) increasingly rely on explicit chain-of-thought (CoT) reasoning to solve complex tasks, yet the safety of the reasoning process itself remains largely unaddressed. Existing work on LLM safety focuses on content safety--detecting harmful, biased, or factually incorrect outputs -- and treats the reasoning chain as an opaque intermediate artifact. We identify reasoning safety as an orthogonal and equally critical security dimension: the requirement that a model's reasoning trajectory be logically consistent, computationally efficient, and resistant to adversarial manipulation. We make three contributions. First, we formally define reasoning safety and introduce a nine-category taxonomy of unsafe reasoning behaviors, covering input parsing errors, reasoning execution errors, and process management errors. Second, we conduct a large-scale prevalence study annotating 4111 reasoning chains from both natural reasoning benchmarks and four adversarial attack methods (reasoning hijacking and denial-of-service), confirming that all nine error types occur in practice and that each attack induces a mechanistically interpretable signature. Third, we propose a Reasoning Safety Monitor: an external LLM-based component that runs in parallel with the target model, inspects each reasoning step in real time via a taxonomy-embedded prompt, and dispatches an interrupt signal upon detecting unsafe behavior. Evaluation on a 450-chain static benchmark shows that our monitor achieves up to 84.88\% step-level localization accuracy and 85.37\% error-type classification accuracy, outperforming hallucination detectors and process reward model baselines by substantial margins. These results demonstrate that reasoning-level monitoring is both necessary and practically achievable, and establish reasoning safety as a foundational concern for the secure deployment of large reasoning models.
中文标题/摘要
标题：超越内容安全：大型语言模型推理漏洞的实时监控
大型语言模型（LLMs）越来越依赖显式的思维链（CoT）推理来解决复杂任务，但推理过程本身的安全性仍然在很大程度上未得到解决。现有的LLM安全工作集中于内容安全——检测有害、偏见或事实不准确的输出——并将推理链视为不透明的中间产物。我们将推理安全识别为一个正交且同样关键的安全维度：模型的推理轨迹必须在逻辑上保持一致、计算上高效，并且抵御对抗性操控。我们做出了三项贡献。首先，我们正式定义了推理安全，并引入了一个涵盖输入解析错误、推理执行错误和过程管理错误的九类不安全推理行为的分类法。其次，我们进行了一项大规模的普遍性研究，注释了来自自然推理基准和四种对抗攻击方法（推理劫持和拒绝服务）的4111条推理链，确认所有九种错误类型在实践中均会发生，并且每种攻击都会产生可机械解释的特征。第三，我们提出了推理安全监控器：一个基于LLM的外部组件，与目标模型并行运行，通过嵌入分类法的提示实时检查每个推理步骤，并在检测到不安全行为时发出中断信号。在450条链的静态基准测试中的评估显示，我们的监控器在步骤级定位准确率上达到84.88%和错误类型分类准确率达到85.37%，显著优于幻觉检测器和过程奖励模型基线。这些结果表明，推理级监控既是必要的，也是可实际实现的，并确立了推理安全作为大型推理模型安全部署的基础性关注点。

This paper contributes by defining reasoning safety, introducing a taxonomy of unsafe reasoning behaviors, and conducting a prevalence study that reveals the occurrence of various reasoning errors in practice. The proposed methodology includes a Reasoning Safety Monitor that operates alongside the target model to inspect reasoning steps in real time and signal unsafe behaviors. Evaluation on a benchmark of 450 reasoning chains demonstrates that the monitor achieves high accuracy in both localization and error classification, indicating that reasoning-level monitoring is essential and feasible for the secure deployment of LLMs.

Enhancing Jailbreak Attacks on LLMs via Persona Prompts
Authors: Zheng Zhang, Peilin Zhao, Deheng Ye, Hao Wang
Venue: NeurIPS 2025
First: 2025-07-28T12:03:22+00:00 · Latest: 2026-03-25T15:46:17+00:00
Comments: Workshop on LLM Persona Modeling at NeurIPS 2025
Abs · PDF · Code1 · Code2 · Code3
Abstract
Jailbreak attacks aim to exploit large language models (LLMs) by inducing them to generate harmful content, thereby revealing their vulnerabilities. Understanding and addressing these attacks is crucial for advancing the field of LLM safety. Previous jailbreak approaches have mainly focused on direct manipulations of harmful intent, with limited attention to the impact of persona prompts. In this study, we systematically explore the efficacy of persona prompts in compromising LLM defenses. We propose a genetic algorithm-based method that automatically crafts persona prompts to bypass LLM's safety mechanisms. Our experiments reveal that: (1) our evolved persona prompts reduce refusal rates by 50-70% across multiple LLMs, and (2) these prompts demonstrate synergistic effects when combined with existing attack methods, increasing success rates by 10-20%. Our code and data are available at https://github.com/CjangCjengh/Generic_Persona.
中文标题/摘要
标题：通过角色提示增强对大型语言模型的越狱攻击
越狱攻击旨在利用大型语言模型（LLMs），诱使其生成有害内容，从而揭示其脆弱性。理解和应对这些攻击对推动LLM安全领域至关重要。以往的越狱方法主要集中在对有害意图的直接操控上，而对角色提示的影响关注较少。在本研究中，我们系统地探讨了角色提示在破坏LLM防御中的有效性。我们提出了一种基于遗传算法的方法，自动生成角色提示以绕过LLM的安全机制。我们的实验表明：（1）我们演化的角色提示使多个LLM的拒绝率降低了50-70%；（2）这些提示与现有攻击方法结合时表现出协同效应，成功率提高了10-20%。我们的代码和数据可在https://github.com/CjangCjengh/Generic_Persona获取。

SafeSeek: Universal Attribution of Safety Circuits in Language Models
Authors: Miao Yu, Siyuan Fu, Moayad Aloqaily, Zhenhong Zhou, Safa Otoum, Xing fan, Kun Wang, Yufei Guo, Qingsong Wen
First: 2026-03-24T14:32:53+00:00 · Latest: 2026-03-24T14:32:53+00:00
Abs · PDF · Code1 · Code2
Abstract
Mechanistic interpretability reveals that safety-critical behaviors (e.g., alignment, jailbreak, backdoor) in Large Language Models (LLMs) are grounded in specialized functional components. However, existing safety attribution methods struggle with generalization and reliability due to their reliance on heuristic, domain-specific metrics and search algorithms. To address this, we propose \ourmethod, a unified safety interpretability framework that identifies functionally complete safety circuits in LLMs via optimization. Unlike methods focusing on isolated heads or neurons, \ourmethod introduces differentiable binary masks to extract multi-granular circuits through gradient descent on safety datasets, while integrates Safety Circuit Tuning to utilize these sparse circuits for efficient safety fine-tuning. We validate \ourmethod in two key scenarios in LLM safety: \textbf{(1) backdoor attacks}, identifying a backdoor circuit with 0.42\% sparsity, whose ablation eradicates the Attack Success Rate (ASR) from 100\% $\to$ 0.4\% while retaining over 99\% general utility; \textbf{(2) safety alignment}, localizing an alignment circuit with 3.03\% heads and 0.79\% neurons, whose removal spikes ASR from 0.8\% $\to$ 96.9\%, whereas excluding this circuit during helpfulness fine-tuning maintains 96.5\% safety retention.
中文标题/摘要
标题：SafeSeek：语言模型中安全电路的通用归因
机械解释性揭示了大型语言模型（LLMs）中安全关键行为（例如，调整、越狱、后门）是基于专门的功能组件。然而，现有的安全归因方法由于依赖启发式、特定领域的指标和搜索算法，难以实现泛化和可靠性。为了解决这个问题，我们提出了\ourmethod，一个统一的安全解释框架，通过优化识别LLMs中的功能完整安全电路。与专注于孤立头部或神经元的方法不同，\ourmethod引入可微分的二进制掩码，通过对安全数据集的梯度下降提取多粒度电路，同时集成安全电路调优，以利用这些稀疏电路进行高效的安全微调。我们在LLM安全的两个关键场景中验证了\ourmethod：\textbf{(1) 后门攻击}，识别出一个稀疏度为0.42\%的后门电路，其消融使攻击成功率（ASR）从100\%降至0.4\%，同时保留超过99\%的通用效用；\textbf{(2) 安全对齐}，定位一个稀疏度为3.03\%的对齐电路和0.79\%的神经元，其移除使ASR从0.8\%激增至96.9\%，而在有用性微调中排除该电路则保持96.5\%的安全保留。

Previous safety attribution methods have been limited by their reliance on heuristic, domain-specific metrics and search algorithms, leading to issues with generalization and reliability. The proposed method, SafeSeek, offers a unified safety interpretability framework that utilizes optimization to identify functionally complete safety circuits in LLMs, employing differentiable binary masks for multi-granular circuit extraction and integrating Safety Circuit Tuning for efficient safety fine-tuning. This approach has been validated in two scenarios: it successfully identifies a backdoor circuit with minimal sparsity, significantly reducing the Attack Success Rate while maintaining general utility, and localizes an alignment circuit whose removal drastically increases the Attack Success Rate, demonstrating its effectiveness in enhancing safety in LLMs.

DriveSafe: A Hierarchical Risk Taxonomy for Safety-Critical LLM-Based Driving Assistants
Authors: Abhishek Kumar, Riya Tapwal, Carsten Maple
First: 2026-01-17T18:50:47+00:00 · Latest: 2026-03-23T18:19:05+00:00
Comments: This is the revised version of the paper
Abs · PDF · Code1 · Code2
Abstract
Large Language Models (LLMs) are increasingly integrated into vehicle-based digital assistants, where unsafe, ambiguous, or legally incorrect responses can lead to serious safety, ethical, and regulatory consequences. Despite growing interest in LLM safety, existing taxonomies and evaluation frameworks remain largely general-purpose and fail to capture the domain-specific risks inherent to real-world driving scenarios. In this paper, we introduce DriveSafe, a hierarchical, four-level risk taxonomy designed to systematically characterize safety-critical failure modes of LLM-based driving assistants. The taxonomy comprises 129 fine-grained atomic risk categories spanning technical, legal, societal, and ethical dimensions, grounded in real-world driving regulations and safety principles and reviewed by domain experts. To validate the safety relevance and realism of the constructed prompts, we evaluate their refusal behavior across six widely deployed LLMs. Our analysis shows that the evaluated models often fail to appropriately refuse unsafe or non-compliant driving-related queries, underscoring the limitations of general-purpose safety alignment in driving contexts.
中文标题/摘要
标题：DriveSafe：安全关键型基于LLM的驾驶助手的分层风险分类法
大型语言模型（LLM）越来越多地集成到基于车辆的数字助手中，其中不安全、模糊或法律上不正确的响应可能导致严重的安全、伦理和监管后果。尽管对LLM安全性的关注日益增加，但现有的分类法和评估框架仍然主要是通用的，未能捕捉到现实驾驶场景中固有的特定领域风险。本文介绍了DriveSafe，一种分层的四级风险分类法，旨在系统地描述基于LLM的驾驶助手的安全关键型故障模式。该分类法包括129个细粒度的原子风险类别，涵盖技术、法律、社会和伦理维度，基于现实驾驶法规和安全原则，并经过领域专家的审查。为了验证构建的提示的安全相关性和现实性，我们评估了六个广泛部署的LLM的拒绝行为。我们的分析表明，被评估的模型往往未能适当地拒绝不安全或不合规的驾驶相关查询，突显了在驾驶环境中通用安全对齐的局限性。

Using LLM-as-a-Judge/Jury to Advance Scalable, Clinically-Validated Safety Evaluations of Model Responses to Users Demonstrating Psychosis
Authors: May Lynn Reese, Markela Zeneli, Mindy Ng, Jacob Haimes, Andreea Damien, Elizabeth Stade
Venue: NeurIPS 2025
First: 2026-03-20T04:31:03+00:00 · Latest: 2026-03-20T04:31:03+00:00
Comments: published at IASEAI 2026, preliminary work presented at GenAI4Health workshop at NeurIPS 2025
Abs · PDF · Code1 · Code2
Abstract
General-purpose Large Language Models (LLMs) are becoming widely adopted by people for mental health support. Yet emerging evidence suggests there are significant risks associated with high-frequency use, particularly for individuals suffering from psychosis, as LLMs may reinforce delusions and hallucinations. Existing evaluations of LLMs in mental health contexts are limited by a lack of clinical validation and scalability of assessment. To address these issues, this research focuses on psychosis as a critical condition for LLM safety evaluation by (1) developing and validating seven clinician-informed safety criteria, (2) constructing a human-consensus dataset, and (3) testing automated assessment using an LLM as an evaluator (LLM-as-a-Judge) or taking the majority vote of several LLM judges (LLM-as-a-Jury). Results indicate that LLM-as-a-Judge aligns closely with the human consensus (Cohen's $κ_{\text{human} \times \text{gemini}} = 0.75$, $κ_{\text{human} \times \text{qwen}} = 0.68$, $κ_{\text{human} \times \text{kimi}} = 0.56$) and that the best judge slightly outperforms LLM-as-a-Jury (Cohen's $κ_{\text{human} \times \text{jury}} = 0.74$). Overall, these findings have promising implications for clinically grounded, scalable methods in LLM safety evaluations for mental health contexts.
中文标题/摘要
标题：使用LLM作为评判者/陪审团推进可扩展的临床验证模型响应用户精神病的安全评估
通用大型语言模型（LLMs）正被广泛应用于心理健康支持。然而，新的证据表明，高频使用存在显著风险，特别是对于精神病患者，因为LLMs可能会强化妄想和幻觉。现有的LLM在心理健康背景下的评估受限于缺乏临床验证和评估的可扩展性。为了解决这些问题，本研究将精神病作为LLM安全评估的关键条件，(1) 开发并验证七个临床知情的安全标准，(2) 构建人类共识数据集，以及(3) 使用LLM作为评估者（LLM作为评判者）或采取多个LLM评判者的多数投票（LLM作为陪审团）进行自动评估。结果表明，LLM作为评判者与人类共识高度一致（Cohen's $κ_{\text{human} \times \text{gemini}} = 0.75$, $κ_{\text{human} \times \text{qwen}} = 0.68$, $κ_{\text{human} \times \text{kimi}} = 0.56$），而最佳评判者的表现略优于LLM作为陪审团（Cohen's $κ_{\text{human} \times \text{jury}} = 0.74$）。总体而言，这些发现对心理健康背景下LLM安全评估的临床基础和可扩展方法具有良好的启示。
Summary / 总结
The research addresses the growing concern regarding the safety of general-purpose Large Language Models (LLMs) in mental health support, particularly for individuals with psychosis, as existing evaluations lack clinical validation and scalability. Previous methods have not adequately assessed the risks of LLMs reinforcing delusions and hallucinations, prompting the authors to propose a novel approach that includes developing seven clinician-informed safety criteria, creating a human-consensus dataset, and employing LLMs as evaluators. This method is well-motivated by the need for clinically validated assessments and demonstrates significant contributions by aligning LLM evaluations with human consensus, achieving high agreement scores (Cohen's κ values) that indicate effective performance. The proposed methodology shows promise for scalable safety evaluations of LLMs in mental health contexts, with results suggesting that LLM-as-a-Judge slightly outperforms LLM-as-a-Jury in assessing safety criteria.
